{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","title":"Gift Guide: 9 security and privacy gifts to keep your friends and family safe","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2073760","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><em>Welcome to TechCrunch&#8217;s 2020 Holiday Gift Guide! Need help with gift ideas? We&#8217;re here to help! We&#8217;ll be rolling out gift guides from now through the end of December. </em><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/pages/gift-guide-2020/\"><em>You can find our other guides right here.</em></a></p>\n<p>For many of us, being home a lot more right now also means being online a lot more. It&#8217;s a great time to evaluate how you&#8217;re keeping your data safe — and to help others in your life do the same.</p>\n<p>Whether it&#8217;s teaching them to use things like physical security keys or just convincing them to stop writing their passwords on sticky notes, there are LOTS of little ways to nudge your friends and family in a safer direction. We&#8217;ve put together an array of gift ideas that&#8217;ll help them keep things locked down without breaking the bank (and, if you&#8217;re the one they&#8217;d call to help clean up after a security incident, probably save you some time in the end).</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Much of what we wrote for <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/27/gift-guide-essential-security-and-privacy-gifts-to-help-protect-your-friends-and-family/\">our 2019 guide</a> still holds true. There are some timeless security essentials that you can&#8217;t miss out on, and we&#8217;ve searched around for the best deals. But we also have a few more fun gift ideas up our sleeves for the holiday season.</p>\n<p><em>This article contains links to affiliate partners where available. When you buy through these links, TechCrunch may earn an affiliate commission.</em></p>\n<h2>Timeless security essentials for your friends and family</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2085611\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2085611\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2085611 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/security-essentials.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"587\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/security-essentials.jpg 1500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/security-essentials.jpg?resize=150,86 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/security-essentials.jpg?resize=300,172 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/security-essentials.jpg?resize=768,440 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/security-essentials.jpg?resize=680,390 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/security-essentials.jpg?resize=50,29 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2085611\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Images from top-left clockwise: Yubico, 1Password, Amazon and Amazon)</p></div></p>\n<h2 id=\"a-password-manager-subscription\">A password manager subscription</h2>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/12/25/cybersecurity-101-guide-password-manager/\">Password managers</a> are a real lifesaver. One strong, unique password lets you into your entire bank of passwords. They&#8217;re great for storing your passwords and other secrets, but also for encouraging you to use better, stronger, unique passwords. And because many are cross-platform, you can bring your passwords with you. Plenty of password managers exist — from <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/11/02/free-lastpass/\">LastPass</a>, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/03/26/mozillas-free-password-manager-firefox-lockbox-launches-on-android/\">Lockbox</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/05/30/dashlane-series-d/\">Dashlane</a>, to open-source versions like KeePass. Many are free, but a premium subscription often comes with benefits and better features. And if you&#8217;re a journalist, 1Password has <a href=\"https://1password.com/for-journalism/\">a free subscription</a> just for you.</p>\n<p><strong>Price:</strong> Many free; premium offerings start at $36 &#8211; $45 annually<br />\n<strong>Available from:</strong> <a href=\"https://1password.com/sign-up/\">1Password</a> | <a href=\"https://lastpass.com/premium/payment\">LastPass</a> | <a href=\"https://www.dashlane.com/plans\">Dashlane</a> | <a href=\"https://keepass.info/\">KeePass</a></p>\n<h2>Don&#8217;t forget about a physical two-factor key</h2>\n<p>Your online accounts have everything about you and you&#8217;d want to keep them safe. A security key is a physical hardware device that offers far greater protections than a two-factor code going to your phone. A security key plugs into your USB port on your computer (or <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/20/yubikey-dual-usb-c-lightning/\">the charging port on your phone</a>) to &#8220;prove&#8221; to online services, like Facebook, Google and Twitter, that you are who you say you are. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/01/08/yubico-launches-a-new-nfc-security-key-and-preps-iphone-support/\">YubiKeys</a> are by far our favorite and come in all shapes and sizes. The latest YubiKey 5 series has something for everyone, no matter what kind of devices they have. They&#8217;re also cheap. Google also has a range of its own branded <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/10/14/google-titan-security-key-usb-c/\">Titan security keys</a>, one of which also offers Bluetooth connectivity.</p>\n<p><strong>Price:</strong> From $25 &#8211; $55, depending on device type, from <a href=\"https://www.yubico.com/products/compare-yubikey-5-series/\">Yubico Store</a> or <a href=\"https://store.google.com/product/titan_security_key\">Google Store</a></p>\n<h2 id=\"a-webcam-cover-to-hide-your-modesty\">A webcam cover to protect your privacy</h2>\n<p>We&#8217;re all living through this pandemic together, and most of us are still working from home. If you, like me, have accidentally <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/08/sorry-i-gatecrashed-your-zoom-meeting/\">joined a video call by mistake</a>, you&#8217;ll be more thankful for your webcam cover than you could ever know. Webcam covers slide open when you need to access your camera, and slides to cover the lens when you don&#8217;t. It&#8217;s that easy. You can buy webcam covers from practically anywhere — just make sure you get a thin cover that supports your device so as to not damage its display when you close the lid. You can support local businesses and nonprofits — you can search for unique and interesting webcam covers on Etsy or from your favorite internet rights group.</p>\n<p><strong>Price:</strong> from $5 &#8211; $10.<br />\n<strong>Available from:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.etsy.com/market/webcam_covers\">Etsy</a> | <a href=\"https://supporters.eff.org/shop/laptop-camera-cover-set-ii\">Electronic Frontier Foundation</a></p>\n<h2 id=\"a-microphone-blocker\">A microphone blocker to prevent hot mics (and malware)</h2>\n<p>Now that you have your webcam cover, what about your microphone? Just as hackers can tap into your webcam, they can also pick up on your audio. Microphone blockers contain a semiconductor that tricks your computer or device into thinking that it&#8217;s a working microphone, when in fact it&#8217;s not able to pick up any audio. Anyone hacking into your device won&#8217;t hear a thing. Some modern Macs already come with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/10/30/apple-t2-security-chip-microphone-eavesdropping/\">a new Apple T2 security chip</a> which prevents hackers from snooping on your microphone when your laptop&#8217;s lid is shut. But a microphone blocker will work all the time, even when the lid is open.</p>\n<p><strong>Price:</strong> from <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B01LPQJGA2/ref=as_li_qf_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=techcrunchgg-20&#38;creative=9325&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;creativeASIN=B01LPQJGA2&#38;linkId=e78b907f7bb41f37fbd6a0478aa177aa\">$7</a> &#8211; <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B07V9T14N3/ref=as_li_qf_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=techcrunchgg-20&#38;creative=9325&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;creativeASIN=B07V9T14N3&#38;linkId=3b38295afe79ddde59bc38485389254d\">$20</a> on Amazon</p>\n<hr />\n<h1>More gifts for the security and privacy minded</h1>\n<h2 id=\"pi-hole-to-block-pesky-ads-and-online-trackers\">A Pi-hole to block pesky ads and online trackers</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073779\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073779\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2073779 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/pi-hole.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"555\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/pi-hole.jpg 1500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/pi-hole.jpg?resize=150,81 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/pi-hole.jpg?resize=300,163 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/pi-hole.jpg?resize=768,416 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/pi-hole.jpg?resize=680,369 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/pi-hole.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2073779\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Image: Pi-hole)</p></div></p>\n<p>Think of a Pi-hole as a &#8220;hardware ad-blocker.&#8221; A Pi-hole is a modified Raspberry Pi mini-computer that runs ad-blocking technology as a box that sits on your network. It means that everyone on your home network benefits from ad blocking. Online ads generate revenue for websites but are also <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/05/22/apple-online-ads-private/\">notorious for tracking users</a> across the web. Until ads can behave properly, a Pi-hole is a great way to capture and sinkhole bad ad traffic. The hardware may be cheap, but the ad-blocking software is free. Donations to the cause are welcome.</p>\n<p><strong>Price:</strong> from $35.<br />\n<strong>Available from:</strong> <a href=\"https://pi-hole.net/\">Pi-hole</a> | <a href=\"https://www.raspberrypi.org/\">Raspberry Pi</a></p>\n<h2 id=\"a-privacy-screen-for-your-computer-or-phone\">Get your computer or phone a privacy screen</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073785\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073785\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2073785 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/privacy-screen.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"555\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/privacy-screen.jpg 1500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/privacy-screen.jpg?resize=150,81 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/privacy-screen.jpg?resize=300,163 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/privacy-screen.jpg?resize=768,416 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/privacy-screen.jpg?resize=680,369 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/privacy-screen.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2073785\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Image: Amazon)</p></div></p>\n<p>How often have you seen someone&#8217;s private messages or documents as you look over their shoulder, or see them in the next seat over? It&#8217;s not as much of an issue when we&#8217;re all at home — but we&#8217;re also all getting pretty comfortable with having whatever on our screens right now, which might not be the best habit to develop. Privacy screens can help protect you from &#8220;visual hacking.&#8221; These screens make it near-impossible for anyone other than the device user to snoop at what you&#8217;re working on. And, you can get them for all kinds of devices and displays — including phones. But make sure you get the right size!</p>\n<p><strong>Price:</strong> from about $17 and up, depending on display size<br />\n<strong>Available from:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/s?k=privacy+filter&#38;i=computers&#38;ref=nb_sb_noss_2\">Amazon</a></p>\n<h2 id=\"find-a-perfect-fit-with-authentic-hacker-apparel\">Find a perfect fit with authentic hacker apparel</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073782\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073782\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2073782 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/hacker-apparel.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"555\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/hacker-apparel.jpg 1500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/hacker-apparel.jpg?resize=150,81 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/hacker-apparel.jpg?resize=300,163 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/hacker-apparel.jpg?resize=768,416 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/hacker-apparel.jpg?resize=680,369 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/hacker-apparel.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2073782\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Image: Zero Day Clothing)</p></div></p>\n<p>Ditch the stereotypical hacker hoodie and get some decent hacker apparel instead. <a href=\"https://www.zerodayclothing.com/index.php\">Zero Day Clothing</a> has some excellent t-shirts and other clothing for your hacker or security-minded friends, from celebrating <a href=\"https://www.zerodayclothing.com/products/diffieloveshellman/diffieloveshellman.php\">Diffie-Hellman</a> encryption, <a href=\"https://www.zerodayclothing.com/products/botnet/botnet.php\">fearing the botnet</a> or designing your own — there&#8217;s something for everyone. We&#8217;re particularly a fan because the company <a href=\"https://www.zerodayclothing.com/faq.php\">supports</a> a ton of causes, from net neutrality all the way to freedom of speech and LGBTQ+ rights and fair access to knowledge and education.</p>\n<p><strong>Available from:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.zerodayclothing.com/\">Zero Day Clothing</a></p>\n<h2 id=\"a-raspberry-pi-400-computer-for-tinkering\">A Raspberry Pi 400 computer for tinkering</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073778\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073778\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2073778 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/raspberry-pi-400.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"555\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/raspberry-pi-400.jpg 1500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/raspberry-pi-400.jpg?resize=150,81 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/raspberry-pi-400.jpg?resize=300,163 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/raspberry-pi-400.jpg?resize=768,416 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/raspberry-pi-400.jpg?resize=680,369 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/raspberry-pi-400.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2073778\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Image: Romain Dillet/TechCrunch)</p></div></p>\n<p>The micro-computer maker has a new product, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/02/raspberry-pi-foundation-announces-the-cute-little-raspberry-pi-400/\">the Raspberry Pi 400</a>, a personal computer kit built into a keyboard and mouse. Connect it to a display and you can get started almost immediately. The device is more powerful than a Chromebook, and allows you to build, develop and tinker to your heart&#8217;s content.</p>\n<p><strong>Price:</strong> $70<br />\n<strong>Available from:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.raspberrypi.org/products/raspberry-pi-400/\">Raspberry Pi</a></p>\n<h2 id=\"test-your-hacker-skills-with-the-backdoors-breaches-card-game\">Test your hacker skills with the Backdoors &#38; Breaches card game</h2>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2073775\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2073775\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2073775 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/backdoors-breaches-1.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"555\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/backdoors-breaches-1.jpg 1500w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/backdoors-breaches-1.jpg?resize=150,81 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/backdoors-breaches-1.jpg?resize=300,163 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/backdoors-breaches-1.jpg?resize=768,416 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/backdoors-breaches-1.jpg?resize=680,369 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/backdoors-breaches-1.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2073775\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">(Image: Black Hills Infosec)</p></div></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.blackhillsinfosec.com/projects/backdoorsandbreaches/\">Backdoors &#38; Breaches</a> is a security-focused card game, developed by <a href=\"https://www.blackhillsinfosec.com/\">Black Hills Infosec</a>, designed to help you conduct incident response exercises while learning about attack tactics, tools and techniques. It&#8217;s a great way to learn more about how to respond after a breach. Don&#8217;t worry if you can&#8217;t play in person any time soon — you can still play virtually, thanks to an active Discord channel.</p>\n<p><strong>Available from:</strong> <a href=\"https://spearphish-general-store.myshopify.com/products/backdoors-breaches-core-deck\">Shopify</a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/pages/gift-guide-2020/\"><img id=\"speakable-summary\">Hyundai takes a controlling stake in an iconic robotics company, Twitter acquires a screen-sharing startup and we round up some security-themed gift ideas. This is your Daily Crunch for December 11, 2020.</p>\n<p><strong>The big story: Hyundai acquires 80% stake in Boston Robotics</strong></p>\n<p>Boston Robotics is behind a number of impressive robots, including the dog-like quadruped Spot. Over the past decade, it&#8217;s changed ownership several times, with Google acquiring it in 2013, then selling it to Japanese investment giant SoftBank in 2017.</p><div id=\"speakable-summary\">French startup <a href=\"https://www.inemotion.com/en/\">In&#38;motion</a> has raised a $12 million (€10 million) funding round led by Upfront Ventures, with 360 Capital also participating. The company has been working on wearable airbag systems for motorbikes.</p>\n<p>Integrated in a vest, the airbag is completely autonomous and can detect crashes in 60 milliseconds. The company has worked on a device called the In&#38;box that analyzes movements in real time. Thanks to different sensors, the device can determine when it’s time to activate the airbag.</p>\n<p>In&#38;motion has worked on different profiles for different types of activities. For instance, if you’re riding a motorcycle on a MotoGP track, chances are you’re going to move faster and change your trajectory quite often. You can choose between traditional motorcycle riding, track and off-road.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Professional racers are increasingly using airbag systems. In addition to MotoGP racers, participants in the 2021 Dakar Rallye will have to use airbags.</p>\n<p>The go-to-market strategy is interesting as the startup isn’t selling its system directly to end users. In&#38;motion has partnered with existing motorcycle brands so they can integrate the system in some vests. This way, In&#38;motion doesn’t have to build out a network of resellers from scratch. So far, the company has sold tens of thousands of systems.</p>\n<p>There’s also a <a href=\"https://www.inemotion.com/myinemotion/en/moto-membership\">subscription component</a>, with unlimited warranty and the ability to replace the In&#38;box device with a new model after three years.</p>\n<p>With today’s funding round, the company wants to expand beyond its home country with a focus on Germany and the U.S. The company plans to double the size of its team.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2086064\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img For the past half century, space exploration and technology has been earth-centric. We’ve studied the earth, orbited the earth and sent images of distant places back to earth. In the coming decade, we’ll embark on a new commitment: We’re going to space to stay. We’re committing to space commerce, space habitation and space exploration in order to not just stay in space, but to extend our human footprint into this solar system. To be successful, we need bold people and new technology to build and deploy the next generation of space capabilities. We need to capture these space opportunities, avoid potential threats and deliver on the promise of a multi-planet human race. This session showcases our partners USC and MIT, as they provide insight into their space programs. They are joined by university partners UCLA, ASU and Caltech, showcasing a range of emerging space technologies. This session will provide an overview of In-Q-Tel as a whole, as well as a discussion of the firm’s activities in the commercial space sector.</p>\n<p><strong>11:00 &#8211; 11:30 a.m.</strong></p>\n<p><strong><span class=\"schedule-item__title\">Fast Money — Enabling a dual-use business model with Defense Innovation Unit (DIU)</span></strong></p>\n<p>Learn how you can take a part of DIU’s development of on-demand access to space, persistent satellite capabilities and broadband space data transfer</p>\n<p><strong>11:30 &#8211; 12:30 p.m.</strong></p>\n<p><strong>Starburst x TechCrunch — Pitch Me to the Moon:</strong> Starburst Aerospace and TechCrunch are teaming up to launch a pitch competition like no other – Pitch Me to the Moon. Think &#8220;Startup Battlefield,&#8221; but for space. Ten promising early-stage space startups (selected by Starburst) will have an opportunity to present their innovations live to a panel of high-profile judges from across the industry.</p>\n<p><strong>1:00 &#8211; 1:50 p.m.</strong><br />\nSponsored by <a href=\"https://aerospace.org/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">The Aerospace Corporation</a></p>\n<p><strong><span class=\"schedule-item__title\">University Showcase — Boldly Innovating in Space, for Space (Part Two)</span></strong></p>\n<p>Bold Missions &#8212; For the past half century, space exploration and technology has been earth-centric. We’ve studied the earth, orbited the earth and sent images of distant places back to earth. In the coming decade, we’ll embark on a new commitment: We’re going to space to stay. We’re committing to space commerce, space habitation and space exploration in order to not just stay in space, but to extend our human footprint into this solar system. To be successful, we need bold people and new technology to build and deploy the next generation of space capabilities. We need to capture these space opportunities, avoid potential threats and deliver on the promise of a multi-planet human race. This session showcases our partners USC and MIT, as they provide insight into their space programs. They are joined by university partners UCLA, ASU and Caltech, showcasing a range of emerging space technologies. Working with the Aerospace Corporation, these emerging capabilities can be evaluated and integrated into government space-faring missions for communicating, navigating, and exploring in space with NASA, NOAA and the Air Force.</p>\n<p>Whew, talk about a great lineup. You might say it’s out-of-this-world — which raises the question: Can you hear a rimshot in space? class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/twitter\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"twitter\">Twitter <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> announced that it is acquiring <a href=\"https://squadapp.io/\">Squad</a> and that the team from the screen-sharing social app will be joining Twitter&#8217;s ranks. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/squad-2\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"squad-2\">Squad&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> co-founders, CEO Esther Crawford and CTO Ethan Sutin, and the rest of the team will be coming aboard inside Twitter&#8217;s design, engineering and product departments, Twitter tells us. Crawford specifically notes that she will be leading a product in the conversations space.</p>\n<p>What isn&#8217;t coming aboard is the actual Squad app, which allowed users to share their screens on mobile or desktop and simultaneously video chat, a feature that aimed to find the friend use case in screen-sharing beyond the enterprise use case of presenting. The app will be shutting down tomorrow, Twitter confirms, an unwelcome surprise for its user base largely made up of teen girls.</p>\n<p>Twitter declined to share further terms of the deal.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2086110\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2086110\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2086110 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/1_rEcHcBU_Fmu7PSbh6lwJkA.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"298\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/1_rEcHcBU_Fmu7PSbh6lwJkA.png 2000w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/1_rEcHcBU_Fmu7PSbh6lwJkA.png?resize=150,66 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/1_rEcHcBU_Fmu7PSbh6lwJkA.png?resize=300,131 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/1_rEcHcBU_Fmu7PSbh6lwJkA.png?resize=768,336 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/1_rEcHcBU_Fmu7PSbh6lwJkA.png?resize=680,298 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/1_rEcHcBU_Fmu7PSbh6lwJkA.png?resize=1536,673 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/1_rEcHcBU_Fmu7PSbh6lwJkA.png?resize=50,22 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2086110\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image via Twitter</p></div></p>\n<p>The app&#8217;s functionality seems like a natural fit for the service, though the company did not confirm whether any tech was coming aboard as part of the deal. Twitter hasn&#8217;t been keen to keep separate apps functioning outside of the core Twitter app. Vine was infamously shut down, upsetting users who likely later rallied behind TikTok, a massive success story and perhaps one of the biggest missed opportunities for American social media companies. Meanwhile, Periscope which has largely bumbled along over the years, is in a particularly fragile place with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/11/twitter-app-code-indicates-that-live-video-broadcasting-app-periscope-may-get-shut-down/\">app code emerging </a>just today that indicates an impending shutdown for the app.</p>\n<p>Squad was notably partnered closely with <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/snapchat\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"snapchat\">Snap <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and was an early adopter of many of the company&#8217;s Snap Kit developer tools. Building so much of the app using Snap&#8217;s developer tools could have made porting the tech to Twitter&#8217;s infrastructure a more complicated task, especially when considering how often Snap Kit apps are tied quite closely to the Snapchat user graph.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"zWMpXWdZ1M\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/06/squad-the-anti-bro-startup/\">Squad, the &#8216;anti-bro startup,&#8217; is creating a safe space for teenage girls online</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Squad, the &#8216;anti-bro startup,&#8217; is creating a safe space for teenage girls online&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/06/squad-the-anti-bro-startup/embed/#?secret=zWMpXWdZ1M\" data-secret=\"zWMpXWdZ1M\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Squad raised $7.2 million in venture capital from First Round, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/y-combinator\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"y-combinator\">Y Combinator, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> betaworks, Halogen Ventures, ex-TechCrunch editor <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/alexia-tsotsis\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"alexia-tsotsis\">Alexia Bonatsos&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Dream Machine and a host of other investors. Squad was in the right place at the right time in early 2020. When the pandemic first struck, CEO Esther Crawford told TechCrunch that usage of her app spiked 1,100%.</p>\n<p>Crawford spoke at length about the challenges of scaling a modern social app while avoiding the pitfalls of toxicity that so often seem to come with reaching new heights. In an interview with TechCrunch last year, she told us her team was “trying to learn from the best in what they did but get rid of the shit.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In a <a href=\"https://esthercrawford.medium.com/squad-is-now-part-of-twitter-48dd73891f71\">Medium post</a>, Crawford also took the opportunity of her startup&#8217;s exit to lobby investors to start backing more diverse founders.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I hope that our exit will tip the scale a bit more toward convincing investors to put money into diverse teams because each success is another proof point that we, the historically under-capitalized and underestimated founders, are a good bet,&#8221; Crawford wrote in a Medium post. &#8220;Invest in women and people of color because we will make you money.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"F3kPRr8QLp\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/01/17/squad-screenshare/\">Squad is the id=\"speakable-summary\">This quarter, strong earnings results from public cloud companies were overshadowed by a seemingly <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/10/airbnbs-first-day-pop-caps-off-a-stellar-week-for-tech-ipos/\">endless IPO cycle</a>. Another moment we somewhat missed over the last few weeks was the stock market pushing the value of public cloud companies to all-time highs.</p>\n<p>These events are connected. And they bode well for startups working on SaaS and API-delivered software, which are keeping the climate for cloud venture investment warm and valuations stretched by historical norms.</p>\n<hr />\n<p><strong><em>The Exchange explores startups, markets and money. Read it <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/subscribe/?tpcc=theexchange\">every morning on Extra Crunch</a>, or get <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/newsletters\">The Exchange newsletter</a> every Saturday.</em></strong></p>\n<hr />\n<p>The earnings results that have made Wall Street content include a growing number of cloud companies that are seeing revenue growth accelerate from Q2 2020 to Q3 2020, according to a <a href=\"https://twitter.com/jaminball/status/1337174904861458435\">recent analysis by Redpoint&#8217;s Jamin Ball</a>.</p>\n<p>Astute readers will recall that The Exchange <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/20/why-is-cloud-revenue-growth-so-slow-if-the-digital-transformation-is-accelerating/\">chatted with Ball after the Q2 earnings cycle</a>, a conversation that included puzzling over how to square a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/12/is-the-vaunted-cloud-acceleration-falling-flat/\">nearly uniform deceleration in revenue growth</a> from Q1 to Q2 in the software sector, which, at the very same time, was supposedly <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/05/the-accelerating-digital-transformation-redux/\">undergoing a boom in demand</a> thanks to the pandemic and a suddenly remote workforce.</p>\n<p>One hypothesis Ball offered was that deals signed in Q2 by SaaS companies would not show up much until Q3 if they were signed in the back-half of the quarter. Regardless of the reason, Q3 featured a far-stronger crop of cloud results that imply a strengthening sector.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/subscribe/?tpcc=theexchange\"><img loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignright wp-image-1995213 size-medium\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?w=300\" alt=\"\" width=\"300\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg 900w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=150,150 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=300,300 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=768,768 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=680,680 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=32,32 32w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=50,50 50w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=64,64 64w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=96,96 96w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?resize=128,128 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">For us startup watchers on the hunt for a hint of what is going on in opaque private markets, this is a useful data point. If you&#8217;ve been slightly befuddled as to why the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/18/3-investors-discuss-the-state-of-saas-investing-in-2020/\">venture capital space has seen deals accelerate</a> with time-to-conviction falling from weeks to minutes — and pre-emption the new normal — this is part of the why.</span></p>\n<p>As the future has been pulled forward when it comes to digitizing the American and global economies, it&#8217;s a good time to be a software company. This was visible in SaaS company <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/smartsheet-3\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"smartsheet-3\">Smartsheet&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> earnings this quarter. The Exchange chatted with <a href=\"https://twitter.com/markmader\">CEO Mark Mader</a> about his company&#8217;s recent earnings results that beat expectations and led to the company&#8217;s shares rising. Analyst upgrades have followed.</p>\n<p>This morning, let&#8217;s examine the data regarding how many cloud companies are seeing revenue growth accelerate, dig into Smartsheet&#8217;s results to see what we can learn (hint: SMBs matter), and then apply all our findings to the startup market itself so that we can go into the weekend as informed as possible.</p>\n<h2>Public acceleration</h2>\n<p>At the risk of being cheeky, I&#8217;ve embedded <a href=\"https://twitter.com/jaminball/status/1337174904861458435/photo/1\">Ball&#8217;s chart</a> concerning Q3 revenue acceleration from cloud companies below. (If you are into similar data sets, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/jaminball/\">he&#8217;s worth following on Twitter</a>.) Here&#8217;s the data:</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2086049\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2086049\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2086049 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-9.30.00-AM.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"342\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-9.30.00-AM.png 1001w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-9.30.00-AM.png?resize=150,76 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-9.30.00-AM.png?resize=300,151 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-9.30.00-AM.png?resize=768,387 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-9.30.00-AM.png?resize=680,342 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-9.30.00-AM.png?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2086049\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image: Jamin Ball</p></div></p>\n<p>This chart shows Q2&#8217;s cloud year-over-year growth rates subtracted from Q3&#8217;s own; a result greater than one shows that a company&#8217;s year-over-year growth accelerated from the second quarter to the third. The higher the number of cloud companies that wind up with a result of 1% or greater in the above chart, the faster the cloud market as a whole is accelerating.</p>\n<p><div border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/GtZ-V9Brmaw\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 11 Dec 2020 15:55:34 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?w=300","linkMd5":"68fc7178c5c589f64742eced65e21b86","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn11@2020_4/2020/12/12/07-45-40-601_9086aabfeefee685.webp","destWidth":300,"destHeight":300,"sourceBytes":32544,"destBytes":32544,"author":"Alex Wilhelm","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/exchange-banner-sq-orng.jpg?w=300":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn11@2020_4/2020/12/12/07-45-40-601_9086aabfeefee685.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/Screen-Shot-2020-12-11-at-9.30.00-AM.png?w=680":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn52@2020_3/2020/12/12/07-46-52-587_bb6a1cb09d6350a4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn16@2020_1/2020/12/12/07-45-30-256_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn77@2020_2/2020/12/12/07-46-53-390_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn31@2020_4/2020/12/12/07-46-52-401_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=GtZ-V9Brmaw:hH6lbviQPvA:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn87@2020_3/2020/12/12/07-46-52-433_9cd3216146d191fc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=GtZ-V9Brmaw:hH6lbviQPvA:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn23@2020_4/2020/12/12/07-46-52-394_863dc711f90c516e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn99@2020_3/2020/12/12/07-46-53-434_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/GtZ-V9Brmaw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn5@2020_3/2020/12/12/07-46-52-992_2218d238cf0edba8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1607759129889},{"createdTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","title":"Here comes the Faraday fabric","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2086148","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">You don&#8217;t have to buy into 5G conspiracy theories to think that you could do with a little less radiation in your life. One way of blocking radiation is a Faraday cage, but this is usually a metal mesh of some kind, making everyday use difficult. Researchers at Drexel University have managed to create a Faraday fabric by infusing ordinary cotton with a compound called MXene — meaning your tinfoil hat is about to get a lot comfier.</p>\n<p>Faraday cages work because radiation in radio frequencies is blocked by certain metals, but because of its wavelength, the metal doesn&#8217;t even have to be solid — it can be a solid cage or flexible mesh. Many facilities are lined with materials like this to prevent outside radiation from interfering with sensitive measurements, but recently companies like <a href=\"https://silent-pocket.com/\">Silent Pocket</a> have integrated meshes into bags and cases that totally isolate devices from incoming signals.</p>\n<p>Let&#8217;s be frank here and say that this is definitely paranoia-adjacent. RF radiation is not harmful in the doses and frequencies we get it, and the FCC makes sure no device exceeds certain thresholds. But there&#8217;s also the possibility that your phone or laptop is naively connecting to public Wi-Fi, getting its MAC number skimmed by other devices, and otherwise interacting with the environment in a way you might not like. And honestly&#8230; with the amount of devices emitting radiation right now, who wouldn&#8217;t mind lowering their dose a little, just to be extra sure?</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>That may be much easier to do in the near future, as Yury Gogotsi and his team at the Drexel Nanomaterials Institute, of which he is director, have come up with a way to coat ordinary textile fibers in a metallic compound that makes them effective Faraday cages — but also flexible, durable and washable.</p>\n<p>The material, which they call MXene and is more of a category than a single compound, is useful in lots of ways, and <a href=\"https://nano.materials.drexel.edu/publications/\">the subject of dozens of papers by the team</a> — this is just the most recent application.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We have known for some time that MXene has the ability to block electromagnetic interference better than other materials, but this discovery shows that it can effectively adhere to fabrics and maintain its unique shielding capabilities,&#8221; <a href=\"https://www.eurekalert.org/pub_releases/2020-12/du-ff121120.php\">said Gogotsi in a news release</a>. You can <a href=\"https://www.eurekalert.org/multimedia/pub/251432.php\">see the fabric in action on video here</a>.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2086223\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2086223\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2086223\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"663\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg 2438w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg?resize=150,97 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg?resize=300,194 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg?resize=768,497 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg?resize=680,440 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg?resize=1536,994 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg?resize=2048,1326 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/mxene-2.jpg?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2086223\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Drexel University</p></div></p>\n<p>MXenes are conductive metal-carbon compounds that can be fabricated into all sorts of forms: solid, liquid, even sprays. In this case it&#8217;s a liquid — a solution of tiny MXene flakes that adhere to the fabric quite easily and produce a Faraday effect, blocking 99.9% of RF radiation in tests. After sitting around for a couple years (perhaps forgotten in a lab cupboard) it kept 90% of their effectiveness, and the treated fabric can also be washed and worn safely.</p>\n<p>You wouldn&#8217;t necessarily want to wear a whole suit of the stuff, but this would make it easier for clothing to include an RF-blocking pocket in a jacket, jeans or laptop bag that doesn&#8217;t feel out of place with the other materials. A hat (or underwear) with a layer of this fabric would be a popular item among conspiracy theorists, of course.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s still a ways from showing up on the rack, but Gogotsi was optimistic about its prospects for commercialization, noting that Drexel has multiple patents on the material and its uses. Other ways of infusing fabric with MXenes could lead to clothes that generate and store energy as well.</p>\n<p>You can read more about this particular application of MXenes <a href=\"https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0008622320311982?via%3Dihub#!\">in the journal Carbon</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=SCBqI6fE4ko:Y_KEfrplxhI:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=SCBqI6fE4ko:Y_KEfrplxhI:7Q72WNTAKBA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a Follow him here: <a href=\"https://twitter.com/rheddleston?lang=en\">@rheddleston</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/docsend?lang=en\">@docsend</a> \t</div>\n\t\n\t\t<div class=\"contributor-byline__more-articles\">\n\t\t<span class=\"more-articles-title\">More posts by this contributor</span>\n\t\t<ul class=\"more-articles-list\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/05/what-q2-fundraising-data-tells-us-about-the-rest-of-2020/\">What Q2 fundraising data tells us about the rest of 2020</a></li>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/05/q3-2020-is-primed-to-be-an-intense-shopping-season-for-vcs/\">Q3 2020 is primed to be an intense shopping season for VCs</a></li>\n\t\t\t\t\t</ul>\n\t</div>\n\t</div>\n</div><p id=\"speakable-summary\">At the end of 2019, no one would have predicted what an unpredictable and difficult year it has been for both startups and VCs in the fundraising world. Now we are staring down the end of 2020 and looking toward what we all hope is a better, safer 2021. What will this new year bring? With an end-of-year sprint to close deals, the anticipation of a new presidential administration and the hope of a COVID-19 vaccine on the horizon, startups and VCs know that change is on the horizon — but how much of that change will be positive?</p>\n<p>As 2020 proved, no one can say for sure what 2021 will bring, but I’d like to put a few predictions on the table based on DocSend’s data and research, including the <a href=\"https://www.docsend.com/index/2020-docsend-startup-index/\">DocSend Startup Index</a>, as well as some trends I’ve seen and my own experiences. These predictions center around how we’ll fundraise post-pandemic, how the funding divide may widen for some, what fundraising activity could look like into 2021, a few sectors we think will fare well and will incorporate some tips on how to succeed in the new year, no matter what comes our way.</p>\n<h2>We’ll interact through a mix of the old and the new</h2>\n<p>The pandemic forced all of us to drastically change how we work and interact with colleagues and clients. When the pandemic subsides and vaccines are widely available, in-person meetings and gathering back at the office will definitely resume, but it’s safe to say the old ways of networking and fundraising won’t shift back 100%. Founders and VCs alike have navigated the ups and downs of remote networking and fundraising interactions and will stick to what works and what doesn’t.</p>\n<p>Is traveling to a conference the best way for a founder to have a chance at meeting the VC who is right to support their business? Will a VC want to drive an hour through Bay Area traffic for an in-person status update meeting on their latest investment? Zoom fatigue aside, video conference calls do have some benefits — efficiency, no travel time — although not all meetings are best conducted virtually.</p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--left\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tNo matter what 2021 has in store, founders can still take proactive steps to help them succeed in their fundraising efforts.\t\t\t\t\t</blockquote>\n\t</div>\n\t</p>\n<p>The extent to which businesses go in-person or stick to virtual meetings could depend directly on what round of fundraising they are working toward or have completed. Businesses in the <a href=\"https://try.docsend.com/fundraising-report\">pre-seed round</a> might stick with more Zoom meetings in order to conserve resources.</p>\n<p>Founders in the seed round will likely split between video and in-person meetings as they are under pressure to show traction in this round, as we found in <a href=\"https://try.docsend.com/seed-report-webinar\">our report on seed fundraising</a>, yet will also need to conserve resources and time. For <a href=\"https://try.docsend.com/series-a-fundraising-report-webinar\">Series A</a>, they might have to meet less in person because they have established relationships with their investors. Series B might see more in-person meetings as their business has reached a level of complexity that is difficult to communicate via a deck or video conference.</p>\n<h2>The funding divide may widen days","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2086344","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The U.S. Food and Drug Administration (FDA) has <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/12/11/health/pfizer-vaccine-authorized.html?smtyp=cur&#38;smid=tw-nytimes\">granted an Emergency Use Authorization (EUA) for the COVID-19 vaccine</a> developed by Pfizer and its partner BioNTech, the New York Times first reported on Friday night, and later <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/pfizer-biontech-covid-19-vaccine-is-authorized-in-the-u-s-11607740101?mod=e2tw\">supported by The Wall Street Journal</a>. This EUA follows a recommendation by an independent panel of experts commissioned by the FDA to review Pfizer&#8217;s application and provide a recommendation, which the panel unanimously supported earlier this week.</p>\n<p>Following this authorization, shipment of the vaccine are expected to begin immediately, with 2.9 million doses in the initial shipment order. Patients in the category of highly vulnerable individuals, which include healthcare workers and senior citizens in long-term care facilities, are expected to begin receiving doses within just a few days not was the EUA is granted.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"mrj797kKDw\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/10/fda-panel-recommends-approving-pfizers-covid-19-vaccine-emergency-use-authorization/\">FDA panel recommends approving Pfizer&#8217;s COVID-19 vaccine emergency use authorization</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;FDA panel recommends approving Pfizer&#8217;s COVID-19 vaccine emergency use authorization&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/10/fda-panel-recommends-approving-pfizers-covid-19-vaccine-emergency-use-authorization/embed/#?secret=mrj797kKDw\" data-secret=\"mrj797kKDw\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>This approval isn&#8217;t a full certification by the U.S. therapeutics regulator, but it is an emergency measure that still requires a comprehensive review of the available information supplied by <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/pfizer\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"pfizer\">Pfizer <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> based on its Phase 3 clinical trial, which covered a group of 44,000 volunteer participants. Pfizer found that its vaccine, which is an mRNA-based treatment, was 95% effective in its final analysis of the data resulting form the trial to date – and also found that safety data indicated no significant safety issues in patients who received the vaccine.</p>\n<p>On top of the initial 2.9 million dose order, the U.S. intends to distribute around 25 million doses by the end of 2020, which could result in far fewer people actually vaccinated since the Pfizer course requires two innoculations for maximum efficacy. Most American shouldn&#8217;t expect the vaccine to be available until at least late Q1 or Q2 2021, given the pace of Pfizer&#8217;s production and the U.S. order volume.</p>\n<p>Still, this is a promising first step, and a monumental achievement in terms of vaccine development turnaround time, since it&#8217;s been roughly eight months since work began on the Pfizer vaccine candidate. Moderna has also submitted an EUA for its vaccine candidate, which is also an mRNA treatment (which provides instructions to a person&#8217;s cells to produce effective countermeasures to the virus). That could follow shortly, meaning two vaccines might be available under EUA within the U.S. before the end of the year.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/benchmark\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"benchmark\">Benchmark, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> the storied venture firm, has brought aboard a fifth general partner: 29-year-old Miles Grimshaw, a Yale graduate who joins the outfit from Thrive Capital, where he similarly joined a team of four other partners back in 2013, helping them raise the firm&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/profile/miles-grimshaw/?sh=3622f9f3612c\">fourth and fifth funds</a> (per Forbes).</p>\n<p>From his post as a general partner with New York-based Thrive, Grimshaw had sourced deals in some of today&#8217;s buzziest startups and served on their boards, including Lattice, Mapbox, Benchling and Airtable, getting to know fellow investors at Benchmark in the process.</p>\n<p>He represented Thrive on the board of <a href=\"https://www.benchling.com/\">Benchling</a> &#8212; whose software helps lab scientists manage their biotech research &#8212; with Eric Vishria, a former entrepreneur and operator who joined Benchmark as a general partner in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2014/07/23/eric-vishria-benchmark/\">2014</a>.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Grimshaw also represented Thrive on the board of the cloud collaboration software company <a href=\"https://airtable.com/\">Airtable</a> with Peter Fenton, who became the longest-serving general partner at Benchmark this year, as famed VC Bill Gurley began <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/22/report-bill-gurley-is-stepping-away/\">transitioning out</a> of an active role at the firm. (Fenton was<a href=\"https://www.mercurynews.com/2007/05/11/peter-fenton-prominent-vc-successful-triathlete/\"> poached from Accel</a> back in 2006.)</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"1jiZu67RlR\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/22/report-bill-gurley-is-stepping-away/\">Bill Gurley is stepping away from an active role at Benchmark, 21 years after joining the firm</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Bill Gurley is stepping away from an active role at Benchmark, 21 years after joining the firm&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/22/report-bill-gurley-is-stepping-away/embed/#?secret=1jiZu67RlR\" data-secret=\"1jiZu67RlR\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>And Grimshaw has been serving on a board with Benchmark&#8217;s Sarah Tavel, who was herself <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/05/09/benchmark-just-hired-sarah-tavel-the-first-female-general-partner-in-the-firms-history/\">poached by the firm</a> in 2017, from Greylock. That company is <a href=\"https://supergreat.com/\">Supergreat</a>, a two-year-old, New York-based site for beauty enthusiasts that&#8217;s building a community of visitors who become reviewers, who then become shoppers.</p>\n<p>Supergreat is among Benchmark&#8217;s newest bets. It was announced earlier this month that Benchmark led the startup&#8217;s $6.5 million Series A round.</p>\n<p>Before hiring Grimshaw, Benchmark&#8217;s newest general partner was Chetan Puttagunta, who <a href=\"https://abovethecrowd.com/2018/07/09/benchmarks-newest-general-partner-chetan-puttagunta/\">joined the firm in 2018</a> from New Enterprise Associates, where he spent more than seven years.</p>\n<p>Benchmark has done better than some firms when it comes to succession, even while many of its general partners remain involved in startups long after they move on from the firm&#8217;s day-to-day operations.</p>\n<p>Firm cofounder Bruce Dunlevie, for example, joined the board of WeWork back in 2012. He&#8217;s now part of a <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/legal-us-otc-wework/amid-wework-board-strife-over-softbank-suit-dissident-directors-win-access-to-skadden-discovery-idUSKBN25K2C9\">lawsuit</a> alleging fellow investor WeWork investor SoftBank of breach of contract and breach of fiduciary duty, after SoftBank abandoned a tender offer to buy out earlier shareholders folllowing WeWork&#8217;s pulled IPO last year.</p>\n<p>Reportedly, Matt Cohler &#8212; a former Facebook exec who was left an active role as a general partner with Benchmark <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/2018/10/1/17924540/matt-cohler-benchmark-mitch-lasky\">in 2018 </a>after a decade with the firm &#8212; also helped Benchmark <a href=\"https://www.theinformation.com/articles/benchmark-wins-deal-for-live-shopping-app-popshop-at-100-million-valuation\">secure its spot</a> in summer as the lead Series A investor in Popshop Live, a livestreaming e-commerce platform. According to The Information, to help seal the deal, Cohler agreed to join the startup&#8217;s board of directors.</p>\n<p>In addition to Cohler and Gurley, who&#8217;ve stepped back in recent years, Mitch Lasky, who joined the firm in 2007, also stepped away from its core team in 2018.</p>\n<p>Benchmark made it known this summer that it was looking to bring aboard a fifth partner, one who likely completes the firm&#8217;s roster for now. As Fenton told us in September when he <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/17/benchmarks-peter-fenton-10-to-20-years-of-innovation-just-got-pulled-forward/\">sat down</a> with us at our TechCrunch Disrupt event, Benchmark &#8220;can&#8217;t scale. When we&#8217;ve gotten above six partners, the firm doesn&#8217;t work so well.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Fenton talked at some length about how Benchmark views the composition of its team. We also talked about that WeWork deal. If you&#8217;re curious to learn more, you can watch that interview below.</p>\n<p>\n\t\t<div class=\"embed breakout\" id=\"vidible_div_0\" data-pid=\"56faf851e4b0d3dcac2e081a\"
