Loizos","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn16@2020_1/2020/12/12/07-45-30-256_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn77@2020_2/2020/12/12/07-46-53-390_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn31@2020_4/2020/12/12/07-46-52-401_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Fvb-wFkUVxA:_RY3a1MEqBw:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn42@2020_4/2020/12/12/07-46-52-521_048fb0346da31ec6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Fvb-wFkUVxA:_RY3a1MEqBw:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn20@2020_6/2020/12/12/07-46-52-385_be23687585fd82ca.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn99@2020_3/2020/12/12/07-46-53-434_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/Fvb-wFkUVxA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn89@2020_1/2020/12/12/07-46-52-349_2e7392f38404b3a1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1607759129899},{"createdTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","title":"Europe urged to block Google-Fitbit ahead of major digital policy overhaul","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2085993","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The European Commission must block the <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>-Fitbit merger as a matter of democratic imperative, prominent academic and author Shoshana Zuboff has warned.</p>\n<p>The Harvard professor who wrote the defining book on <a href=\"https://www.publicaffairsbooks.com/titles/shoshana-zuboff/the-age-of-surveillance-capitalism/9781610395694/\">surveillance capitalism</a> has become the latest voice raised against the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/01/google-is-acquiring-fitbit/\">$2.1 billion data+devices deal</a> &#8212; that&#8217;s now been delayed at the regulatory clearance stage for more than a year.</p>\n<p>Others calling for the Google-<a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/fitbit\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"fitbit\">Fitbit <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> acquisition to be blocked &#8212; unless or until robust competition, democratic and human rights safeguards can be baked in &#8212; include <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/27/no-google-fitbit-merger-without-human-rights-remedies-says-amnesty-to-eu/\">Amnesty International</a>; scores of <a href=\"https://newamericadotorg.s3.amazonaws.com/documents/Joint_NGO_Statement_on_Google_Fitbit_merger_final.pdf\">consumer</a>, <a href=\"https://privacyinternational.org/press-release/3750/press-release-privacy-international-calls-googlefitbit-merger-be-blocked\">privacy</a> and digital rights groups across civic society; and the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/02/20/google-gobbling-fitbit-is-a-major-privacy-risk-warns-eu-data-protection-advisor/\">EU&#8217;s very own data protection advisor</a>, to name a few.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>EU regulators are still considering whether or not to greenlight the merger. The deadline for them to make up their minds was recently <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/16/eus-google-fitbit-antitrust-decision-deadline-pushed-into-2021/\">extended into early 2021</a> &#8212; although a decision could come as soon as next week.</p>\n<p>Back in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/04/google-fitbit-deal-to-be-scrutinized-in-europe-over-data-competition-concerns/\">August</a>, the Commission opened an in-depth investigation into the deal &#8212; saying it was concerned it would &#8220;further entrench Google’s market position in the online advertising markets by increasing the already vast amount of data that Google could use for personalisation of the ads it serves and displays&#8221;.</p>\n<p>EU lawmakers have also expressed skepticism over initial concessions offered by Google which suggested storing Fitbit data in a silo that it said would be kept separate from other Google data.</p>\n<p>It also said it would not use Fitbit data for ad targeting &#8212; at least for a time-limited period (though it&#8217;s not clear what exactly it has proposed in Europe). Elsewhere, Australian regulators are also still eyeing the deal &#8212; and recently <a href=\"https://www.afr.com/technology/accc-asks-industry-if-google-s-fitbit-acquisition-plan-will-work-20201130-p56j79\">sought industry feedback</a> on a pledge by Google not to use Fitbit data for ads for 10 years.</p>\n<p>The ACCC published <a href=\"https://www.accc.gov.au/public-registers/mergers-registers/public-informal-merger-reviews/google-llc-proposed-acquisition-of-fitbit-inc\">draft undertakings</a> in November which includes stipulations such as: &#8220;<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Google must not use any Measured Body Data or Health and Fitness Activity Location Data in or for Google Ads&#8221; and that data must be kept separate. </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"GFjt18eGJq\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/27/no-google-fitbit-merger-without-human-rights-remedies-says-amnesty-to-eu/\">No Google-Fitbit merger without human rights remedies, says Amnesty to EU</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;No Google-Fitbit merger without human rights remedies, says Amnesty to EU&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/27/no-google-fitbit-merger-without-human-rights-remedies-says-amnesty-to-eu/embed/#?secret=GFjt18eGJq\" data-secret=\"GFjt18eGJq\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>But Zuboff&#8217;s point is that targeted advertising is just the tip of the vast data-extracting ambitions of surveillance capitalists &#8212; while health data is one of the few personal data fields these digital giants have not yet been able to mine in their usual limitless way.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Any notion of approving the Fitbit acquisition &#8212; based on Google&#8217;s promises not to do something that is anyway an irrelevant thing, to do or not to do &#8212; is a serious mistake,&#8221; she said yesterday, giving the keynote speech at the annual lecture of the EU Parliament&#8217;s Science and Technology Options Assessment (<a href=\"https://www.europarl.europa.eu/stoa/en/home/highlights\">STOA</a>) panel.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Such a decision should be reconsidered immediately. And never again repeated,&#8221; she added.</p>\n<p>A Google spokesman declined to comment on Zuboff&#8217;s remarks &#8212; pointing only to its <a href=\"https://blog.google/around-the-globe/google-europe/update-fitbit/\">blog post</a> from August where it claims the deal is about &#8220;devices not data&#8221;.</p>\n<h2>Beware the &#8220;epistemic coup&#8221;</h2>\n<p>In the STOA lecture, Zuboff articulates a view of tech giants&#8217; uncontrolled extraction and use of data leading to what she described as an &#8220;epistemic coup&#8221; &#8212; where bottomless digitally-enabled data extraction leads to an unprecedented dominance of knowledge by the private sector, generating radical inequalities and full-spectrum harms, as a data-empowered few are able to run roughshod over humanity, democratic values and the rule of law in the name of increasing their profits.</p>\n<p>&#8220;There is no &#8216;attention economy&#8217;; these are effects of a deeper cause &#8212; and that cause is surveillance capitalism&#8217;s economic imperatives. These corporations are not publishers, they are not distributors, they are not merely adtech providers; they are indiscriminate, radically indifferent all-you-can-eat extractors of everything forever, all for the sake of prediction that become more lucrative as they approach certainty,&#8221; she said.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Knowledge at this kind of scale produces a new kind of power over people. This is what data scientists call the shift from monitoring to actuation. Where there&#8217;s actually sufficient data about a machine system to be able to control it remotely. The thing is now it&#8217;s not just the machine systems; it&#8217;s the human systems.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The wide-ranging <a href=\"https://multimedia.europarl.europa.eu/en/panel-for-future-of-science-and-technology-annual-lecture-2020_20201209-1500-SPECIAL-STOA_vd\">keynote is well worth watching in full</a> for how clearly Zuboff articulates why allowing corporates to &#8220;unilaterally claim[&#8230;] private human experience for raw material, bent to the purposes of datafication, computational production and sales&#8221; is terrible for humanity and the (genuine) communities which make up our civilization &#8212; likening it to how uncontrolled extraction of oil for corporate profit has threatened the survival of life on earth, fuelling climate change, biodiversity decline and mass species extinction.</p>\n<p>The nub of the argument is that surveillance capitalism&#8217;s target is <em>human nature itself</em> &#8212; with Zuboff calling out the &#8220;data business&#8221; playbook of &#8220;hidden extraction mechanisms&#8221; which she said are robbing us of the ability to fight back.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Today our nemesis is not, and could never be, mere data or technology &#8212; but rather the extractors, led by a handful of giant corporations: Google, Facebook, Apple, Amazon, Microsoft, to name only the largest, along with their complex, far-reaching ecosystems, these are corporate institutions that have pioneered a new logic of extraction but with a dark and startling twist&#8230; These corporations have placed the defence of their narrow economic self-interest above the interests of individual sovereignty, democracy and humanity itself.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The keynote included a call to action to European lawmakers to step in and reverse what has been allowed to become entrenched at humanity&#8217;s expense.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I am here today because the European Union represents humanity&#8217;s best hope to alter this course before lawless, unprecedented computational concentrations of knowledge and power become as irreversible and poisonous to our societies as the toxic concentrations of carbon dioxide in our atmosphere have become to our earth,&#8221; said Zuboff, adding: &#8220;The idea that we could bequeath both of these cataclysms to our children is intolerable.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"nYOmJcVoTZ\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/04/google-fitbit-deal-to-be-scrutinized-in-europe-over-data-competition-concerns/\">Google-Fitbit deal to be scrutinized in Europe over data competition concerns</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Google-Fitbit deal to be scrutinized in Europe over data competition concerns&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/04/google-fitbit-deal-to-be-scrutinized-in-europe-over-data-competition-concerns/embed/#?secret=nYOmJcVoTZ\" data-secret=\"nYOmJcVoTZ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>EU lawmakers are on the cusp of unveiling a major package of legislative proposals which will update rules for digital services and bring in new requirements for platforms with significant market power.</p>\n<p>The Commission&#8217;s Digital Services Act (DSA) and the Digital Markets Act (DMA) proposals are due to be presented next Tuesday &#8212; the start of a long road of negotiating to turn the policies into EU law.</p>\n<p>It has turned out to be particularly awkward timing for the Commission, in parallel with the Google-Fitbit decision. Not least because a key EVP involved in shaping the new digital strategy, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/margrethe-vestager\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"margrethe-vestager\">Margrethe Vestager, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> is also the competition commissioner &#8212; so she&#8217;s simultaneously tasked with deciding whether to waive the tech giant&#8217;s latest data acquisition through, even as she puts the finishing touches on ex ante rules for gatekeepers that won&#8217;t likely come into force for years.</p>\n<p>Vestager told the EU parliament&#8217;s <a href=\"https://multimedia.europarl.europa.eu/en/committee-on-economic-and-monetary-affairs_20201210-0900-COMMITTEE-ECON_vd\">Committee on Economic and Monetary Affairs</a> this week that the Commission&#8217;s incoming proposals for a major overhaul of digital regulations are necessary to tackle the challenges of the platform economy.</p>\n<p>The scale and the scope of the platform economy is &#8220;unprecedented and it&#8217;s increasing&#8221;, she said, acknowledging that the digitization process has &#8220;given us a concentration of data, intellectual property, capital &#8212; and because of that there&#8217;s a lot of power in the hands of a few global players&#8221;.</p>\n<p>That in turn is making it &#8220;really urgent&#8221; to complement existing EU competition law enforcement with dedicated regulation for digital services and platform giants, said Vestager.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The DSA will propose a clear set of due diligence obligations and operate the e-commerce framework for all Internet services within the EU and the point is to ensure that digital services face no borders within the EU, define clearer responsibilities and accountability for online platforms such as social media and marketplaces,&#8221; she told MEPs &#8212; saying the overarching aim is to ensure consumers have the same protections online as they already do offline.</p>\n<p>The aim of the DMA &#8212; and its incoming list of &#8220;dos and don&#8217;ts&#8221; for platforms that the EU will define as gatekeepers &#8212; is to make sure digital markets &#8220;stay open and contestable&#8221;, and thus to serve consumers in &#8220;the best possible way&#8221;.</p>\n<h2>&#8216;Trust but verify&#8217; via audit authority</h2>\n<p>In her keynote, Zuboff suggested EU regulators should follow two key principles as they consider what to do.</p>\n<p>Firstly, &#8220;trust but verify&#8221; is how to treat with surveillance capitalists &#8212; so no more &#8220;taken at face value&#8221; pledges swallowed naively and later regurgitated under the one-way logic of extraction maximization. (She raised the awkward example of Facebook&#8217;s reversal of an earlier pledge to EU regulators not to combine WhatsApp user data with Facebook data.)</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">&#8220;Secondly we have to keep in mind so often we reduce the harms back to that originating context of targeted advertising &#8212; when in fact this whole economic logic has moved way beyond targeted advertising to many other markets,&#8221; she also said, warning against EU regulators taking too narrow a view on any concessions made by Google as it works to push open another data gate.  </span></p>\n<p>We&#8217;ve reached out to the Commission for comment on Zuboff&#8217;s remarks.</p>\n<p>Zuboff also spoke to concerns that EU regulators don&#8217;t believe they have legal grounds to deny Google-Fitbit.</p>\n<p>&#8220;If the decision to approve Google&#8217;s acquisition of Fitbit was made because of a determination that EU laws are not strong enough to defend the acquisition denial in the European courts then let us please stop talking this minute; let&#8217;s suspend our event while the parliament moves into an emergency session to pass new laws that are strong enough to take this kind of rejection through the courts. Because we need those laws,&#8221; she said.</p>\n<p>It would certainly be ironic if the Commission green-lit the Google-Fitbit merger because it was worried about losing a legal challenge down the line &#8212; given how frequently tech giants resort to legal action to try to thwart the application of existing EU regulations. Not to mention how fiercely these giants lobby against <em>any</em> new regulation or legislative proposal that would dare to put limits on their ability to continue maximizing their data extraction.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"MEOwlUdXbe\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/04/google-pushes-europe-to-limit-gatekeeper-platform-rules/\">Google pushes Europe to limit &#8216;gatekeeper&#8217; platform rules</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Google pushes Europe to limit &#8216;gatekeeper&#8217; platform rules&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/04/google-pushes-europe-to-limit-gatekeeper-platform-rules/embed/#?secret=MEOwlUdXbe\" data-secret=\"MEOwlUdXbe\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Zuboff said the forthcoming DMA &#8220;is the legal instrument to accomplish this necessary lawmaking [against the surveillance capitalists]&#8221;, addressing her remarks to those in the EU who have the power to pass laws.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Make no mistake: This is your opportunity to make a bold intervention to defend democracy against the surveillance capitalists. Faint heartedness is not an option,&#8221; she said, adding that<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> the </span><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">DSA is likewise an essential intervention to </span><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">defend democracy. </span></p>\n<p>&#8220;This is your chance to finally pry open the black box of surveillance capitalism and demand the right of democratic societies to control their own destiny,&#8221; she said, suggesting regulators&#8217; watch word here should be &#8220;audit authority&#8221;.</p>\n<p>Democracy must have audit authority to protection the public just as regulators have done in countless other industries, she added.</p>\n<p>The Google-Fitbit acquisition was raised in a question to Vestager yesterday during a <a href=\"https://multimedia.europarl.europa.eu/en/committee-on-economic-and-monetary-affairs_20201210-0900-COMMITTEE-ECON_vd\">session</a> of the Committee on Economic and Monetary Affairs &#8212; where she was asked what the EU intends to do vis-à-vis health data and competition, given the risk of tech giants gleaning far deeper and more intimate knowledge of users than they&#8217;ve been able to via current data-mining practices.</p>\n<p>Vestager told the committee she couldn&#8217;t comment on the specific merger as the process is ongoing but she said she agreed health data &#8220;are much more precious and much more sensitive&#8221; than other types of commercially exploited data.</p>\n<p>&#8220;This is why one has to be very careful when it comes to health data and advertising &#8212; because here it can be a much more vulnerable position for the person in question,&#8221; she said.</p>\n<p>&#8220;For health data as such I think it&#8217;s very important that the market develops because the more health data that becomes available the more services people expect for the market to provide for them to have a better understanding of how their health develops,&#8221; she went on, adding on Google-Fitbit specifically that &#8220;it remains to be seen how the remedies were to bear out if they were to be accepted&#8221;.</p>\n<h2>U.S. versus EU approach to antitrust</h2>\n<p>During the session Vestager also faced a number of questions from MEPs about the difference of approach to antitrust between the EU and the U.S. &#8212; where states have just opened a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/09/facebook-antitrust-state-attorneys-general/\">massive antitrust case against Facebook</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"75eQH82Yhe\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/09/facebook-antitrust-state-attorneys-general/\">Facebook hit with massive antitrust lawsuit from 46 states</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook hit with massive antitrust lawsuit from 46 states&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/09/facebook-antitrust-state-attorneys-general/embed/#?secret=75eQH82Yhe\" data-secret=\"75eQH82Yhe\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>She repeatedly stressed that Europe has a &#8220;different&#8221; approach to competition law versus the U.S., sounding a tad on the defensive.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The U.S. Facebook case is a different approach than what we have. In Europe we do not have a ban of monopolies. They have a different legal basis in the U.S. We would say you&#8217;re more than welcome to be successful but with success comes responsibility &#8212; which is why we have article 102 [against abusing a dominant position],&#8221; she said.</p>\n<p>&#8220;As a last resort in Europe we would also be able to ask our [institutions] to split up companies but then we would also have to prove that this was the only thing to solve a competition problem and I don&#8217;t think we have been there yet,&#8221; Vestager added.</p>\n<p>Responding to other questions from MEPs she described her department as doing its &#8220;best&#8221; across a number of big tech investigations &#8212; pointing it&#8217;s recently opened case against Amazon and has others ongoing into Google&#8217;s and Facebook&#8217;s use of data for advertising.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We have a couple of ongoing investigations into the Facebook ecosystem &#8212; on the use of data from customers and consumers into advertising and how the Facebook marketplace is functioning,&#8221; she noted.</p>\n<p>&#8220;These cases are not as advanced as they are in the U.S. when it comes to Facebook but I find [the U.S. action] very encouraging,&#8221; she added, saying it&#8217;s a sign that &#8220;the global debate about tech dominance has been shifting over the last couple of years&#8221;.</p>\n<p>Asked about Facebook&#8217;s reversal of an earlier promise not to combine Facebook and WhatsApp user data, Vestager said EU regulators had performed an analysis at the time &#8212; looking into whether such a move would still allow for competition &#8212; and &#8220;found there would be room for others services of the same kind&#8221;.</p>\n<p>There were no follow-up questions in the event format so MEPs were unable to ask whether Vestager believes that analysis was sound or flawed. But it&#8217;s not a good look that the EU&#8217;s competition authorities were left so wrong-footed on Facebook&#8217;s market power.</p>\n<p>Off her own bat, Vestager merely said: &#8220;It remains to be seen what will be the outcome of the U.S. [Facebook antitrust] case; as I said they have a different legal basis &#8212; to see if by acquiring this company you have entrenched monopoly position.&#8221;</p>\n<p>She was also asked what the Commission intends to do about companies using self-serving tactics to artificially prolong investigations (and thus delay competition enforcement) &#8212; such as by procrastinating or handing out requested information only with substantial delay.</p>\n<p>Vestager said its approach is to aim to &#8220;always try to balance things out&#8221; but she argued it&#8217;s important to give businesses enough time to respond properly even though it extends the length of investigations.</p>\n<p>During the session she did also note that the aim for the DMA is to enable competition authorities to be &#8220;so much quicker&#8221; &#8212; because the ex ante rules will bake in &#8220;self-executing obligations&#8221;.</p>\n<p>The gatekeeper status also means regulators will not need to do the work of establishing dominance first &#8212; &#8220;<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">which means you&#8217;ll get to the sanction must faster and should prevent damages in the marketplace&#8221;, she noted. </span></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s not clear whether or not the forthcoming legislative package will feature a new competition tool for specifically tackling digital markets &#8212; which the Commission consulted on earlier this year.</p>\n<p>Reports have suggested this has been dropped after a standard EU pre-regulatory review process. But the commissioner did not confirm either way.</p>\n<p>She was also asked about interim measures &#8212; an existing tool she dusted off <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/10/16/europe-issues-interim-antitrust-order-against-broadcom-as-probe-continues/\">last year</a> after an extended period when it had not been used, applying it in a case against chipmaker Broadcom.</p>\n<p>On this she said the tool has been shown to have been useful &#8212; noting the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/07/european-antitrust-regulators-settle-with-broadcom-a-year-after-interim-measures-flex/\">Broadcom case was settled in a year</a> (which is a very speedy turnaround for a competition case) &#8212; and she suggested the tool could be used more frequently in the future. &#8220;<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">I think that we will see we can use it more often,&#8221; she told the MEPs. </span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qqqlNnvhvO\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/30/big-techs-blackbox-algorithms-face-regulatory-oversight-under-eu-plan/\">Big tech&#8217;s &#8216;blackbox&#8217; algorithms face regulatory oversight under EU plan</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Big tech&#8217;s &#8216;blackbox&#8217; algorithms face regulatory oversight under EU plan&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/30/big-techs-blackbox-algorithms-face-regulatory-oversight-under-eu-plan/embed/#?secret=qqqlNnvhvO\" data-secret=\"qqqlNnvhvO\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/7foVHM_En80\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 11 Dec 2020 15:07:27 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"e798c3bcdb45c338be05e6f77d30de48","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn16@2020_1/2020/12/12/07-45-30-256_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Natasha Lomas","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn16@2020_1/2020/12/12/07-45-30-256_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn77@2020_2/2020/12/12/07-46-53-390_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn31@2020_4/2020/12/12/07-46-52-401_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=7foVHM_En80:vGfRrJHmbjQ:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn40@2020_2/2020/12/12/07-46-52-384_02bbe5b72abeeea2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=7foVHM_En80:vGfRrJHmbjQ:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn29@2020_5/2020/12/12/07-46-53-334_df6dc3be094f3768.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn99@2020_3/2020/12/12/07-46-53-434_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/7foVHM_En80":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn13@2020_1/2020/12/12/07-46-53-170_cb318d7749b53c79.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1607759129900},{"createdTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","title":"Oracle is headed to Texas now, too","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2086253","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Austinites, watch out; another tech company is headed into town.</p>\n<p>Just days after Tesla CEO Elon Musk revealed during an interview that he has <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/elon-musk-to-discuss-teslas-banner-year-despite-pandemic-silicon-valleys-future-11607449988\">moved to Texas</a>, and less than two weeks after HP Enterprise, a spin-out of the iconic Silicon Valley company Hewlett-Packard, announced that it is separately <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/houston-california-greg-abbott-texas-1ce5ef41c6e20e84b5954de11fa3c8a7\">moving to Texas</a>, yet another of the Bay Area&#8217;s best-known brands &#8212; Oracle &#8212;  is pulling up stakes and headed east to Texas, too.</p>\n<p>The news was first reported by <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-12-11/oracle-moves-headquarters-to-texas-joins-exodus-from-california?utm_source=google&#38;utm_medium=bd&#38;cmpId=google\">Bloomberg</a>. Oracle confirmed the move in a statement sent to TechCrunch, saying that along with a &#8220;more flexible employee work location policy,&#8221; the company has changed its corporate headquarters from Redwood Shores, California, to Austin. &#8220;We believe these moves best position <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/oracle\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"oracle\">Oracle <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> for growth and provide our personnel with more flexibility about where and how they work.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>A spokeswoman declined to answer more questions related to the move, but Oracle says that &#8220;many&#8221; of its employees can choose their office location, as well as continue to work from home part time or full time.</p>\n<p>HPE and Oracle aren&#8217;t the first major tech companies to plot such moves in recent times. Late last year, the brokerage giant <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/charles-schwab\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"charles-schwab\">Charles Schwab <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> said it was <a href=\"https://www.dallasnews.com/business/2019/11/30/schwab-is-the-latest-company-leaving-california-for-texas-and-it-wont-be-the-last-expert-says/\">leaving the Bay Area for Texas </a>as it was announcing its $26 billion merger with TD Ameritrade, though it chose Dallas, about 200 miles away from Austin.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"TJ64LZ6VF7\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/08/elon-musk-has-made-the-move-to-texas/\">Elon Musk moved to Texas</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Elon Musk moved to Texas&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/08/elon-musk-has-made-the-move-to-texas/embed/#?secret=TJ64LZ6VF7\" data-secret=\"TJ64LZ6VF7\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Tech giants <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Google have also been expanding their presence in the state. Apple announced in 2018 that it was building a <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2018/12/13/business/apple-austin-campus.html\">$1 billion campus</a> in Austin. Meanwhile, Google, which opened its first Austin office 13 years ago, said last year that it was beginning to lease <a href=\"https://www.statesman.com/news/20190614/google-says-it-plans-significant-expansion-in-austin\">far more space</a> in the city.</p>\n<p>Taxes, a more affordable cost of living for employees, a lower cost of doing business and less competition for talent are among the top drivers for the companies&#8217; moves, though there is also a growing sense that culture is a factor, as well.</p>\n<p>While California is led by Democrats, Texas is led by Republicans, and as the divide between the two parties grows, so does the divide between their respective supporters, with even self-described centrists saying they feel alienated.</p>\n<p>Oracle co-founder and Chairman Larry Ellison has notably been one of few top tech execs to openly support President Donald Trump.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Joe Lonsdale, a co-founder of the venture firm 8VC and Palantir Technologies (which itself recently headed to Denver from Palo Alto), recently explained his own move this year to Texas from California <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/california-love-it-and-leave-it-11605472619\">in the WSJ</a>, writing: &#8220;Politics in the state is in many ways closed off to different ideas. We grew weary of California’s intolerant far left, which would rather demonize opponents than discuss honest differences of opinion.&#8221;</p>\n<p>This fall, in conversation with reporter Kara Swisher, Musk suggested he was also outside of Democratic circles, describing his political views as &#8220;socially very liberal and then economically right of center, maybe, or center? I don&#8217;t know. <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/09/28/opinion/sway-kara-swisher-elon-musk.html\">Obviously I&#8217;m not a communist.</a>&#8221;</p>\n<p>While Austin is becoming a go-to spot for many of California&#8217;s wealthiest contrarians, others are headed to Florida. Coincidentally or not, Florida is another Republican-controlled state that, like Texas, does not collect state tax.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/keith-rabois\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"keith-rabois\">Keith Rabois, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> a Founders Fund investor who recently left the Bay Area for Miami, contributed to the <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/outsidespending/contrib_all.php?cmte=C00610907&#38;type=A&#38;cycle=2016\">NeverTrump PAC</a> in 2016 and said his first choice for U.S. president this year was Democratic contender Pete Buttigieg. But he has also worried openly about democratic socialism, of which the GOP has <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2020/08/25/905895428/republicans-blast-democrats-as-socialists-heres-what-socialism-is\">long accused</a> Democrats of promoting.</p>\n<p>Venture capitalist <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/david-blumberg\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"david-blumberg\">David Blumberg, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> a Trump supporter, is also headed to Miami, he announced recently. Blumberg said he had it with &#8220;poor governance at the local level in San Francisco and statewide in California.&#8221; Yet he seemed to have grown frustrated with the Bay Area some time ago.</p>\n<p>As Blumberg <a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https://www.vox.com/recode/2019/9/17/20869679/donald-trump-silicon-valley-fundraiser-2020\">told Vox last year, </a>he believes that tech platforms are biased against conservatives. He also told the outlet that the Valley was home to many more Trump supporters than might be imagined, and that &#8220;we generally keep our heads down” because “people who go out publicly for Republicans and for Trump can get business banned or get blackballed.”</p>\n<p>Impetus notwithstanding, a longer-term question is whether these moves &#8212; particular for those individuals and smaller outfits that are relocating &#8212; will prove permanent.</p>\n<p>At least one tech exec, Twitter and Medium co-founder Ev Williams, has returned to the Bay Area after moving away &#8212; in his case, to New York. Williams, who was largely &#8220;looking for a change,&#8221; made the move with his family late last year after spending 20 years in the Bay Area, he <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/24/talking-techs-exodus-twitters-new-labels-and-mediums-future-with-founder-ev-williams/\">recently told</a> TechCrunch. Then COVID struck.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I had never lived in New York and thought, ‘Why not go? Now seems like a good time.’ Turns out I was wrong. [Laughs.] It was a very bad time to move to New York.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"CkWSmfM0i3\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/24/talking-techs-exodus-twitters-new-labels-and-mediums-future-with-founder-ev-williams/\">Talking tech&#8217;s exodus, Twitter&#8217;s labels and Medium&#8217;s next moves with founder Ev Williams</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Talking tech&#8217;s exodus, A","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2086021","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"http://gorillasapp.com\">Gorillas</a>, a grocery delivery startup that operates its own hyper local fulfillment centers and has already been a hit in Berlin, has raised $44 million in Series A funding.</p>\n<p>Probably one of European tech&#8217;s worst kept secrets this year, the round is led by hedge fund Coatue, with participation from other unnamed European investors. Coatue’s Daniel Senft and Bennett Siegel will join Gorillas‘ board.</p>\n<p>Noteworthy, Accel and Index were <a href=\"https://www.deutsche-startups.de/2020/11/02/dealmonitor-02-11-2020/\">reportedly</a> in the running, but ultimately didn’t invest. Atlantic Food Labs previously backed Gorillas in a seed round thought to be around €1.2 million.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Founded by Kağan Sümer and Jörg Kattner in May this year and operating in Berlin and Cologne, Gorillas delivers groceries within an average of ten minutes. Unlike gig economy models, it employs riders directly and is emphasising its ability to get fresh groceries, along with other household items, to shoppers at very short notice and at “retail prices”. The idea is that the startup can address a large part of the groceries market that falls outside of a weekly bulk shop.</p>\n<p>Some have dubbed the model that Gorillas is attempting to make work, &#8220;dark&#8221; convenience stores, in reference to the dark kitchens that run on top of Deliveroo and UberEats and operate as delivery only restaurants. In this instance, Gorillas and other European competitors, such as Dija (which we reported is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/24/dija/\">closing its own large funding round</a>) and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/05/london-based-weezy-raises-seed/\">Weezy</a>, are building out local delivery only grocery/convenience stores. These startups are also often compared to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/gopuff-funding/\">goPuff</a> in the U.S.</p>\n<p>Gorillas CEO Kağan Sümer says that mass supermarkets, including their delivery models, are designed so that the consumer organises their grocery shopping around the needs of the supermarket and supply chain, rather than the supermarket being designed around the needs of the consumer.</p>\n<p>This sees an emphasis on long shelf life products, where even fresh goods are treated for longer expiry dates, and a model that serves the weekly bulk shop well, but at the detriment of two other use-cases: “emergency” shopping, such as when you’re missing a key ingredient, or quickly replenishing your fridge based on what you fancy consuming right now.</p>\n<p>“The biggest problem is that bulk purchases are super served. What I mean by that is this: all of the supermarket infrastructure is shaped around bulk purchases,” Sümer tells me, arguing that this leaves one third of the market underserved.</p>\n<p>“You have penne but no Arrabiata; how do you get that sauce that you need now? [There is] no way.</p>\n<p>“So we asked ourselves, what would happen if a company pops up and serves people with what they need when they need it? Our hypothesis was that people would appreciate it and shift their interaction with groceries to more on demand purchases”.</p>\n<p>With a slogan that reads: “Faster than you,” and a delivery fee of just €1.80, one question mark over Gorillas (and others in the space) is if the unit economics can ever stack up, especially at scale and if the company really isn’t marking up prices significantly. “Through our procurement relationships, we have healthy margins which allow us to sell at retail prices,” says Sümer, pushing back. “Taking into account the solid basket sizes and procurement margins we are able to build a long-term sustainable business”.</p>\n<p>He says the average delivery time is 10 minutes. “Through our network of centrally located fulfillment centers we are able to service customers in a small delivery radius. Ultimately we strive to deliver an efficient and fast service with full transparency on delivery times,” adds the Gorillas CEO.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Gorillas says the new funding will be used for expansion across Germany and will accelerate its rollout across more of Europe &#8212; first stop, Amsterdam. Additionally, the company will use the capital to build out its team in Berlin. More ambitious, by the end of Q2 next year, Gorillas says it plans to be available in over 15 cities in Germany and across Europe, operating over 60 fulfillment centers.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s67KOt4oNY\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/24/dija/\">Dija, a new delivery startup from former Deliveroo employees, is closing in on a $20M round led by Blossom</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Dija, a new delivery ringing","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2084867","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">In case you missed it: A ransomware attack saw patient data stolen from one of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/26/us-fertility-ransomware-attack/\">the largest U.S. fertility networks</a>; the Supreme Court began hearing a case that may change <a week&#8217;s Decrypted, we&#8217;re deep-diving into two stories beyond the headlines, including why the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/12/08/cybersecurity-firm-fireeye-says-it-was-hacked-by-a-nation-state/\">breach at cybersecurity giant FireEye</a> has the cybersecurity industry in shock.</p>\n<hr />\n<h2 id=\"the-big-picture\">THE BIG PICTURE</h2>\n<h3 id=\"google-researcher-finds-a-major-iphone-security-bug-now-fixed\">Google researcher finds a major iPhone security bug, now fixed</h3>\n<p>What happens when you leave one of the best security researchers alone for six months? You get one of the most devastating vulnerabilities ever found in an iPhone — a bug so damaging that it can be exploited over-the-air and requires no interaction on the user&#8217;s part.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2084868\" style=\"width: 910px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2084868\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2084868\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/google-project-zero-iphones.gif\" alt=\"\" width=\"900\" height=\"506\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2084868\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The AWDL bug under attack using a proof-of-concept exploit developed by a Google researcher. <strong>Image Credits:</strong> Ian Beer/<a href=\"https://googleprojectzero.blogspot.com/2020/12/an-ios-zero-click-radio-proximity.html\">Google Project Zero</a></p></div></p>\n<p>The vulnerability was found in <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Wireless Direct Link (AWDL), an important part of the iPhone&#8217;s software that among other things allows users to share files and photos over Wi-Fi through Apple&#8217;s AirDrop feature.</p>\n<p>&#8220;AWDL is enabled by default, exposing a large and complex attack surface to everyone in radio proximity,&#8221; wrote <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a href=\"https://twitter.com/i41nbeer/status/1333884909858004992\">Ian Beer</a> in a tweet, who found the vulnerability in November and disclosed it to Apple, which pushed out a <a href=\"https://support.apple.com/en-us/HT210918\">fix for iPhones</a> and <a href=\"https://support.apple.com/en-us/HT210919\">Macs</a> in January.</p>\n<p>But exploiting the bug allowed Beer to gain access to the underlying iPhone software using Wi-Fi to gain control of a vulnerable device — including the messages, emails and photos — as well as the camera and microphone — without alerting the user. Beer said that the bug could be exploited over &#8220;hundreds of meters or more,&#8221; depending on the hardware used to carry out the attack. But the good news is that <a href=\"https://googleprojectzero.blogspot.com/2020/12/an-ios-zero-click-radio-proximity.html\">there&#8217;s no evidence</a> that malicious hackers have actively tried to exploit the bug.</p>\n<p>News of the bug drew immediate attention, though Apple didn&#8217;t comment. NSA&#8217;s Rob Joyce said <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RGB_Lights/status/1333928951941566468?s=20\">the bug</a> find is &#8220;quite an accomplishment,&#8221; given that most iOS bugs require chaining multiple vulnerabilities together in order to get access to the underlying software.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Wow. An iOS exploit that doesn’t involve chaining multiple vulnerabilities together is quite an accomplishment. <a href=\"https://t.co/ZccMcVTIch\">https://t.co/ZccMcVTIch</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Rob Joyce 15:45:29","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","title":"Twitter app code indicates that live video broadcasting app Periscope may get shut down","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2085999","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/twitter\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"twitter\">Twitter <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has been doubling down on video services within its app, building out Twitter Live and recently launching <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/17/twitter-rolls-out-stories-aka-fleets-to-all-users-will-also-test-a-clubhouse-rival/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Fleets</a> so that users can share more moving media alongside their pithy 180-word observations, links and still photos. But in the process, it appears that it may also be streamlining its bigger stable of services. Code in the Twitter app indicates that Periscope &#8212; the live video broadcasting app that launched a thousand fluttering hearts &#8212; may be headed into retirement.</p>\n<p>Date and other details are still unknown, but super-sleuth developer Jane Machun Wong <a href=\"https://twitter.com/wongmjane/status/1337344129995395073\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">found a line</a> in Twitter&#8217;s app code that indicated a link to a shutdown notice for Periscope (which currently does not go to a live link).</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">This text found inside Twitter’s app indicates the shutdown notice might be shown in future versions of the Periscope app, directing users to a FAQ page about the app <a href=\"https://t.co/gGrNNxRLL7\">pic.twitter.com/gGrNNxRLL7</a></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8212; Jane Manchun Wong (@wongmjane) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/wongmjane/status/1337344129995395073?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">December 11, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p>There are no shutdown references in any of the code in the currently obtainable version of the Persicope app, Wong told us, but she also pointed out that the two apps do share some code &#8212; indeed there are integrations between the two Twitter-owned apps &#8212; and &#8220;I guess [that] is how the text in the screenshot got slipped into Twitter,&#8221; she said.</p>\n<p>We are reaching out to Twitter for a response to her discovery and will update as we learn more.</p>\n<p>If this does play out with Periscope getting retired, it would be the end of a five-year run for the app.</p>\n<p>Twitter <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/03/13/how-periscope-works/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">acquired Periscope</a> before it had even launched (we <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/03/04/twitter-in-talks-with-live-streaming-app-periscope/?_ga=2.101545153.1912869610.1607285587-2020914112.1606652257\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">broke the news</a> of the acquisition before that), as part of a bold move to double down on video, and specifically live video. At the time, the move was coming as Twitter was really coming into its own as a platform for media companies, &#8220;citizen journalists&#8221; and simply people who wanted to get the word out more widely on whatever they were thinking about or doing.</p>\n<p>At the time, Twitter was also eyeing up and apparently <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/04/12/this-stream-aint-big-enough-for-the-both-of-us/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">trying to stem the viral growth</a> of Meerkat, &#8220;the&#8221; app of 2015. That was not going to be an issue for the long run, though. Eventually Meerkat, either because of Periscope or because of the cyclical nature of hype, did <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/09/30/meerkat-star-of-2015-is-officially-dead/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">fizzle out</a>, only to relaunch as interactive video chat app <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/11/21/the-internet-third-place/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Houseparty</a>, which eventually got noticed by Fortnite maker Epic, who <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/12/fortnite-maker-epic-acquires-social-video-app-houseparty/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">then bought it</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"StuMMGJX3W\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/12/fortnite-maker-epic-acquires-social-video-app-houseparty/\">Fortnite maker Epic acquires social video app Houseparty</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Fortnite maker Epic acquires social video app Houseparty&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/12/fortnite-maker-epic-acquires-social-video-app-houseparty/embed/#?secret=StuMMGJX3W\" data-secret=\"StuMMGJX3W\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Periscope, meanwhile, took a different route as part of Twitter from the very start of its launched life.</p>\n<p>It remained a standalone app, but its team, and specifically founder Kayvon Beykpour, became a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/06/29/twitter-gets-a-re-org-and-new-product-head/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">central part of all of Twitter&#8217;s product development</a>.</p>\n<p>And the central feature of Periscope was the app became a native part of the Twitter app; <a href=\"https://blog.twitter.com/en_us/a/2016/go-live-on-twitter.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Twitter Live</a> &#8220;powered by Periscope,&#8221; which has been <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/03/21/in-push-for-more-live-video-twitter-officially-announces-the-producer-api/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">expanded with API access</a> and other <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/03/29/twitter-makes-it-easier-to-share-the-right-part-of-a-live-video-with-launch-of-timestamps/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">features</a>. Twitter itself promotes Twitter Live content, not Periscope&#8217;s: you can follow <a href=\"https://twitter.com/twitterlive\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">@TwitterLive</a> to get highlights of some of the people and organizations using the live feature in the app. (Other leading social apps like Instagram and Facebook have taken a similar route, offering live video features but more as embedded parts of the main platforms, rather than standalone apps where live is front and center.)</p>\n<p>Periscope, you might say, has in the meantime been dying a slow death as a standalone brand and app. But it&#8217;s not a new story: my former (missed!) colleague Josh pointed out <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/12/14/hindscope-is-20-20/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">it was sinking</a> at the end of 2016.</p>\n<p>Still, it&#8217;s just about been bobbing along. <a href=\"https://www.appannie.com/apps/ios/app/972909677/app-ranking?app_slug=972909677&#38;market_slug=ios&#38;device=iphone&#38;type=ranks&#38;date=2020-12-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">AppAnnie&#8217;s rankings</a> indicate that it&#8217;s essentially among the top 100 social networking apps in most markets &#8212; maybe not a bad figure considering how big app stores are now &#8212; although when looking at overall rankings, Periscope is generally too low to register in any major markets.</p>\n<p>Indeed, it&#8217;s definitely not an app that has much buzz, not least because of its owner being popular, but also because video fads have taken a different, TikTok-style turn of late.</p>\n<p>The TikTok effect is an interesting one to consider here. Earlier this year it was reported that Twitter was among those interested in <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/twitter-tiktok-have-held-preliminary-talks-about-possible-combination-11596925449\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">potentially acquiring TikTok</a> when the popular app, owned by China&#8217;s ByteDance, found itself in some regulatory hot water over national security interests (that is a different story, still playing out and seemingly in limbo right now). Some of the apparent reasoning for Twitter&#8217;s interest? It never really got past its <a href=\"https://gizmodo.com/haunted-by-regret-over-killing-vine-twitter-purportedl-1844667451\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">regret</a> over killing off Vine.</p>\n<p>Vine, if you recall, was the popular short-form video app that Twitter <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2012/10/09/if-twitter-gets-into-the-video-hosting-game-it-could-be-a-wonderful-and-horrible-thing/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">acquired</a>, grew <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2013/04/08/just-six-months-after-being-acquired-twitters-vine-hits-1-free-spot-on-apples-app-store/?_ga=2.21372859.1070664616.1607334007-209244718.1579131500\">really well for a while</a> as it saw it gain some entertaining virality, but <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/10/27/twitter-is-shutting-down-vine/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">then shut down</a> to focus more attention on &#8212; yep &#8212; Periscope.</p>\n<p>Many in retrospect have wondered &#8220;what could have been&#8221; had Twitter held on to Vine and put the effort and investment into building it out. (Or indeed, what could have happened <a href=\"https://twitter.com/rus/status/791681274339622913?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E791681274339622913%7Ctwgr%5E%7Ctwcon%5Es1_&#38;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Ftechcrunch.com%2F2016%2F10%2F27%2Ftwitter-is-shutting-down-vine%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">if it never sold to Twitter in the first place</a>, but that is also a different story.)</p>\n<p>If Periscope sinking away is on the cards, it&#8217;s a question that probably still bears asking &#8212; what could have been? Even with live video within Twitter&#8217;s app, it&#8217;s not the star of the show. One can&#8217;t help but wonder if live video might next appear front and center elsewhere, made by a different company, much like short-form video finally had its day in a ByteDance way.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"A6Z4KThhAc\"><p><a founders","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2085545","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/general-catalyst-partners\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"general-catalyst-partners\">General Catalyst <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has made early bets on some of the biggest companies in tech today, including Airbnb, Lemonade and Warby Parker.</p>\n<p>We sat down with <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/katherine-boyle\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"katherine-boyle\">Katherine Boyle <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Peter Boyce, who co-lead the firm&#8217;s seed-stage investments, to discuss what they look for in founders, which sectors they&#8217;re most excited about and how business has changed in the wake of the COVID-19 pandemic.</p>\n<p>This conversation is part of our broader <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/16/announcing-the-extra-crunch-live-event-series/\">Extra Crunch Live series</a>, where we sit down with VCs and founders to discuss startup core competencies and get advice. We&#8217;ve spoken to folks like Aileen Lee, Mark Cuban, Roelof Botha, Charles Hudson and many, others. You can browse the <a href=\"http://techcrunch.com/ecl\">full library of episodes here</a>.</p>\n<p>Check out our full conversation with Boyce and Boyle in the YouTube video below, or skim the text for the highlights.</p>\n<h2>Which personality traits are most important in founders</h2>\n<p><strong>Katherine Boyle:</strong> I look for what I would call this obsessive trait, where they are learning more about the regulatory complications, where they are constantly trying to figure out how to solve a problem.</p>\n<p>I&#8217;d say that the common theme among the founders that I support are that they have this sort of obsessive gene or personality, where they will go deeper and deeper and deeper. When we invest in these companies, it becomes very clear that they often have sort of a contrarian view of the industry. Maybe they are not industry-native. They come at it from a different perspective of problem solving. They&#8217;ve had to defend that thesis for a very, very long time in front of a variety of different customers and different people. In some ways, that makes them much stronger in terms of the way they approach problems.</p>\n<p><strong>Peter Boyce:</strong> I think the first would be being magnetic for talent. It ends up influencing the speed of learning and development. Really incredible founding teams that can be magnetic for talent and learning just kind of spirals out of control in really good ways over time. I really look for the speed and the sources of learning. And can folks be really intentional? Can they get the right set of advisors and teammates around them?</p>\n<p>The second would be the personal connection to the problem space. It&#8217;s like there&#8217;s this kind of deep-seated source of energy and fuel that actually isn&#8217;t going to run out. Catherine and I&#8217;ve been lucky to work across a number of different particular thematic areas, but the thing they have in common is just this personal connection to how and why their business needs to exist. Because I just think that that fuel doesn&#8217;t run out, you know what I mean? Like, that&#8217;s renewable.</p>\n<h2>On fundraising and building trust remotely</h2>\n<p><strong>Boyle:</strong> If you&#8217;re someone who&#8217;s comfortable presenting on Zoom, making connections on Zoom, or using Signal and using Twitter and being very online, then I 100% think that you can make investments, build community and build connections through digital worlds and digital platforms. If you really like that in-person connectivity, then you might consider staying in a tech hub, or you might consider sort of these distanced walks until things go back to normal. <div 15:45:29","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","title":"Hyundai buys controlling interest in Boston Dynamics","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2085203","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It’s official. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/boston-dynamics\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"boston-dynamics\">Boston Dynamics <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> is becoming part of the Hyundai family (pending regulatory approval, naturally). The Waltham, Massachusetts-based robot maker confirmed in <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/hyundai-motor-group-to-acquire-controlling-interest-in-boston-dynamics-from-softbank-group-opening-a-new-chapter-in-the-robotics-and-mobility-industry-301191028.html\">a press release</a> today that the South Korean technology company is acquiring controlling interest. The deal, which values the company at $1.1 billion, gives Hyundai Motor Group an 80% stake, with SoftBank controlling the remaining 20%.</p>\n<p>The transaction marks the Spot-maker’s third change of hands in a mere seven years. After nearly a quarter-century operating as a research firm (with some big financial help from organizations like DARPA), it sold to Google in 2013, becoming part of a new robotics wing led by then-executive Andy Rubin.</p>\n<p>After Google X Robotics was largely dissolved, Boston Dynamics changed hands in 2017, becoming a subsidiary of Japanese investment giant <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/softbank\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"softbank\">SoftBank <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>. It was an odd fit for the company, and a rough year for SoftBank likely hasn’t helped matters. At the very least, Hyundai is a more logical home for the company, after being owned by a firm whose best-known robot is Pepper, the humanoid hospitality &#8216;bot.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"iSxz07VGq1\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/hyundai-reportedly-in-talks-to-buy-softbank-owned-boston-dynamics/\">Hyundai reportedly in talks to buy SoftBank-owned Boston Dynamics</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Hyundai reportedly in talks to buy SoftBank-owned Boston Dynamics&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/hyundai-reportedly-in-talks-to-buy-softbank-owned-boston-dynamics/embed/#?secret=iSxz07VGq1\" data-secret=\"iSxz07VGq1\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>As we noted while reporting on earlier rumors about the acquisition, Hyundai has been making some big investments in the category. The list includes a recent joint venture with Aptiv to commercialize autonomous driving systems. There’s also the recently announced ultimate mobility vehicles, or UMV &#8212; a borderline sci-fi vehicle with legs.</p>\n<p>“Boston Dynamics’ commercial business has grown rapidly as we&#8217;ve brought to market the first robot that can automate repetitive and dangerous tasks in workplaces designed for human-level mobility,&#8221; CEO Rob Playter said in a release tied to the deal. &#8220;We and Hyundai share a view of the transformational power of mobility and look forward to working together to accelerate our plans to enable the world with cutting edge automation, and to continue to solve the world’s hardest robotics challenges for our customers.”</p>\n<p>Boston Dynamics, of course, has been blurring the lines between science fiction and reality for several decades now. More recently, however, it’s taken a much stronger interest in commercializing its advanced technologies. Under SoftBank, the company launched Spot, a quadruped robot that draws on years of robotic innovation, including the iconic Big Dog.</p>\n<p>Spot went up for sale last year in limited quantities. It’s now available for anyone in the U.S. with $74,500 burning a hole in their pocket. The company is also pushing to commercialize its wheeled Handle robot for warehouse and fulfillment related purposes. That robot is due out some time next year. While the sophistication and resulting price tags for the company’s robots have drawn a fair bit of skepticism, investors have taken increased interest in robots and automation firms in the wake of year-long COVID-19-related shutdowns.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Hyundai Motor Group will provide Boston Dynamics a strategic partner affording access to Hyundai Motor Group’s in-house manufacturing capability and cost benefits stemming from efficiencies of scale,&#8221; according to the release. &#8220;Boston Dynamics will benefit substantially from new capital, technology, affiliated customers, and Hyundai Motor Group’s global market reach enhancing commercialization opportunity for its robot products.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The deal is expected to close in by June.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"SmuMBj3xv2\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/24/boston-dynamics-puts-its-robotic-quadruped-spot-up-for-sale/\">Boston 15:45:29","updatedTime":"2020-12-12 15:45:29","title":"Cloud-gaming platforms were 2020’s most overhyped trend","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2081039","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It was an unprecedented year for [insert anything under the sun], and while plenty of tech verticals saw shifts that warped business models and shifted user habits, the gaming industry experienced plenty of new ideas in 2020. However, the loudest trends don&#8217;t always take hold as predicted.</p>\n<p>This year, Google, Microsoft, Facebook and Amazon each leaned hard into new cloud-streaming tech that shifts game processing and computing to cloud-based servers, allowing users to play graphics-intensive content on low-powered systems or play titles without dealing with lengthy downloads.</p>\n<p>It was heralded by executives as a tectonic shift for gaming, one that would democratize access to the next generation of titles. But in taking a closer look at the products built around this tech, it&#8217;s hard to see a future where any of these subscription services succeed.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Massive year-over-year changes in gaming are rare because even if a historically unique platform launches or is unveiled, it takes time for a critical mass of developers to congregate and adopt something new — and longer for users to coalesce. As a result, even in a year where major console makers launch historically powerful hardware, massive tech giants pump cash into new cloud-streaming tech and gamers log more hours collectively than ever before, it can feel like not much has shifted.</span></p>\n<p>That said, the gaming industry did push boundaries in 2020, though it&#8217;s unclear where meaningful ground was gained. The most ambitious drives were toward redesigning marketplaces in the image of video streaming networks, aiming to make a more coordinated move toward driving subscription growth and moving farther away from an industry defined for decades by one-time purchases structured around single-player storylines, one dramatically shaped by internet networking and instantaneous payments infrastructure software.</p>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--pullout block--left\">\n\t\t<blockquote>\n\t\t\tToday&#8217;s products are far from dead ends for what the broader industry does with the technology.\t\t\t\t\t</blockquote>\n\t</div>\n\t</p>\n<p>But shifting gamers farther away from one-off purchases wasn&#8217;t even the gaming industry&#8217;s most fundamental reconsideration of the year, a space reserved for a coordinated move by the world&#8217;s richest companies to upend the console wars with an invisible competitor. It&#8217;s perhaps unsurprising that the most full-featured plays in this arena are coming from the cloud services triumvirate, with Google, Microsoft and Amazon each making significant strides in recent months.</p>\n<p>The driving force for this change is both the maturation of virtual desktop streaming and continued developer movement toward online cross-play between gaming platforms, a trend long resisted by legacy platform owners intent on maintaining siloed network effects that pushed gamers toward buying the same consoles that their friends owned.</p>\n<p>The cross-play trend reached a fever pitch in recent years as entities like <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/epic-games-2\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"epic-games-2\">Epic Games&#8217; <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Fortnite developed massive user bases that gave developers exceptional influence over the deals they struck with platform owners.</p>\n<p>While a trend toward deeper cross-play planted the seeds for new corporate players in the gaming world, it has been the tech companies with the deepest pockets that have pioneered the most concerted plays to side-load a third-party candidate into the console wars.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s already clear to plenty of gamers that even in their nascent stages, cloud-gaming platforms aren&#8217;t meeting up to their hype and standalone efforts aren&#8217;t technologically stunning enough to make up for the apparent lack of selection in the content libraries.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=w6-o2QAiAJ0:32O7doWznMA:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img
